<!--StartFragment--><p data-start="0" data-end="370">Electrical engineering and electronics documentation frequently require the use of mathematical formulas to explain electrical behavior, circuit analysis, and power calculations. Modern document formatting systems can accurately render these formulas using LaTeX-based mathematical formatting, making technical reports and academic papers more professional and readable.</p>
<p data-start="372" data-end="459">One of the fundamental formulas in electrical engineering is Ohm’s Law, represented as</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mi>V</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>I</mi><mi>R</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">V = IR</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">V</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">I</span><span class="mord mathnormal">R</span></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="499" data-end="816">, where voltage is equal to the product of current and resistance. This equation is widely used in circuit analysis and electrical calculations. Another important formula is electrical power calculation, expressed as <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>P</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>V</mi><mi>I</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">P = VI</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">P</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">V</span><span class="mord mathnormal">I</span></span></span></span></span>, which determines the power consumed in an electrical circuit.</p>
<p data-start="818" data-end="919">In alternating current (AC) systems, frequency and angular velocity are related through the equation</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mi>ω</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>2</mn><mi>π</mi><mi>f</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\omega = 2\pi f</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">ω</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mord mathnormal">π</span><span class="mord mathnormal">f</span></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="959" data-end="1214">, where angular frequency depends on the signal frequency. Capacitor behavior in electronic circuits can be represented using the capacitance equation <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>Q</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>C</mi><mi>V</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Q = CV</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">C</span><span class="mord mathnormal">V</span></span></span></span></span>, where electric charge is proportional to capacitance and voltage.</p>
<p data-start="1216" data-end="1500">Electrical energy calculations are also important in power systems and are commonly represented as <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>E</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>P</mi><mi>t</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">E = Pt</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">E</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Pt</span></span></span></span></span>, where energy depends on power consumption over time. In electromagnetic systems, force between electric charges is described using Coulomb’s Law:</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" encoding="application/x-tex">F = k\frac{q_1 q_2}{r^2}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">F</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">k</span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">r</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span <p data-start="1540" data-end="1693">. These mathematical expressions are essential in electrical engineering education, research papers, circuit design reports, and technical documentation.</p>

<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="V = IR"></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>

Modern document formatting systems can accurately render these formulas using LaTeX-based mathematical formatting, making technical reports and academic papers more professional and readable.</p>
<p data-start="372" data-end="459">One of the fundamental formulas in electrical engineering is Ohm’s Law, represented as</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="V = IR"></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="499" data-end="816">, where voltage is equal to the product of current and resistance. This equation is widely used in circuit analysis and electrical calculations. Another important formula is electrical power calculation, expressed as <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="P = VI"></span></span></span></span>, which determines the power consumed in an electrical circuit.</p>
<p data-start="818" data-end="919">In alternating current (AC) systems, frequency and angular velocity are related through the equation</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="\omega = 2\pi f"></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="959" data-end="1214">, where angular frequency depends on the signal frequency. Capacitor behavior in electronic circuits can be represented using the capacitance equation <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="Q = CV"></span></span></span></span>, where electric charge is proportional to capacitance and voltage.</p>
<p data-start="1216" data-end="1500">Electrical energy calculations are also important in power systems and are commonly represented as <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="E = Pt"></span></span></span></span>, where energy depends on power consumption over time. In electromagnetic systems, force between electric charges is described using Coulomb’s Law:</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="F = k\frac{q_1 q_2}{r^2}"></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="1540" data-end="1693">. These mathematical expressions are essential in electrical engineering education, research papers, circuit design reports, and technical documentation.</p>

<p data-start="1216" data-end="1500">Electrical energy calculations are also important in power systems and are commonly represented as <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>E</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>P</mi><mi>t</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">E = Pt</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">E</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Pt</span></span></span></span></span>, where energy depends on power consumption over time. In electromagnetic systems, force between electric charges is described using Coulomb’s Law:</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math <p data-start="1540" data-end="1693">. These mathematical expressions are essential in electrical engineering education, research papers, circuit design reports, and technical documentation.</p>

<!--StartFragment--><p data-start="0" data-end="370">Electrical engineering and electronics documentation frequently require the use of mathematical formulas to explain electrical behavior, circuit analysis, and power calculations. Modern document formatting systems can accurately render these formulas using LaTeX-based mathematical formatting, making technical reports and academic papers more professional and readable.</p>
<p data-start="372" data-end="459">One of the fundamental formulas in electrical engineering is Ohm’s Law, represented as</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="V = IR"></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="499" data-end="816">, where voltage is equal to the product of current and resistance. This equation is widely used in circuit analysis and electrical calculations. Another important formula is electrical power calculation, expressed as <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="P = VI"></span></span></span></span>, which determines the power consumed in an electrical circuit.</p>
<p data-start="818" data-end="919">In alternating current (AC) systems, frequency and angular velocity are related through the equation</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="\omega = 2\pi f"></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="959" data-end="1214">, where angular frequency depends on the signal frequency. Capacitor behavior in electronic circuits can be represented using the capacitance equation <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="Q = CV"></span></span></span></span>, where electric charge is proportional to capacitance and voltage.</p>
<p data-start="1216" data-end="1500">Electrical energy calculations are also important in power systems and are commonly represented as <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="E = Pt"></span></span></span></span>, where energy depends on power consumption over time. In electromagnetic systems, force between electric charges is described using Coulomb’s Law:</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="F = k\frac{q_1 q_2}{r^2}"></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="1540" data-end="1693">. These mathematical expressions are essential in electrical engineering education, research papers, circuit design reports, and technical documentation.</p>

<body>
<!--StartFragment--><p data-start="0" data-end="370">Electrical engineering and electronics documentation frequently require the use of mathematical formulas to explain electrical behavior, circuit analysis, and power calculations. Modern document formatting systems can accurately render these formulas using LaTeX-based mathematical formatting, making technical reports and academic papers more professional and readable.</p>
<p data-start="372" data-end="459">One of the fundamental formulas in electrical engineering is Ohm’s Law, represented as</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mi>V</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>I</mi><mi>R</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">V = IR</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">V</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">I</span><span class="mord mathnormal">R</span></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="499" data-end="816">, where voltage is equal to the product of current and resistance. This equation is widely used in circuit analysis and electrical calculations. Another important formula is electrical power calculation, expressed as <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>P</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>V</mi><mi>I</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">P = VI</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">P</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">V</span><span class="mord mathnormal">I</span></span></span></span></span>, which determines the power consumed in an electrical circuit.</p>
<p data-start="818" data-end="919">In alternating current (AC) systems, frequency and angular velocity are related through the equation</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mi>ω</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>2</mn><mi>π</mi><mi>f</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\omega = 2\pi f</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">ω</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mord mathnormal">π</span><span class="mord mathnormal">f</span></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="959" data-end="1214">, where angular frequency depends on the signal frequency. Capacitor behavior in electronic circuits can be represented using the capacitance equation <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>Q</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>C</mi><mi>V</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Q = CV</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">C</span><span class="mord mathnormal">V</span></span></span></span></span>, where electric charge is proportional to capacitance and voltage.</p>
<p data-start="1216" data-end="1500">Electrical energy calculations are also important in power systems and are commonly represented as <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>E</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>P</mi><mi>t</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">E = Pt</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">E</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Pt</span></span></span></span></span>, where energy depends on power consumption over time. In electromagnetic systems, force between electric charges is described using Coulomb’s Law:</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mi>F</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>k</mi><mfrac><mrow><msub><mi>q</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><msub><mi>q</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><msup><mi>r</mi><mn>2</mn></msup></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">F = k\frac{q_1 q_2}{r^2}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">F</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">k</span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">r</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs <p data-start="1540" data-end="1693">. These mathematical expressions are essential in electrical engineering education, research papers, circuit design reports, and technical documentation.</p>

<p data-start="372" data-end="459">One of the fundamental formulas in electrical engineering is Ohm’s Law, represented as</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="V = IR"></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="499" data-end="816">, where voltage is equal to the product of current and resistance. This equation is widely used in circuit analysis and electrical calculations. Another important formula is electrical power calculation, expressed as <span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="P = VI"></span></span></span></span>, which determines the power consumed in an electrical circuit.</p>
<p data-start="818" data-end="919">In alternating current (AC) systems, frequency and angular velocity are related through the equation</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="\omega = 2\pi f"></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="959" data-end="1214">, where angular frequency depends on the signal frequency. <p data-start="1540" data-end="1693">. These mathematical expressions are essential in electrical engineering education, research papers, circuit design reports, and technical documentation.</p>

<li class="font-claude-response-body whitespace-normal break-words pl-2"><strong>Fundamental Theorem:</strong> <span class="katex" role="math"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msubsup><mo>∫</mo><mi>a</mi><mi>b</mi></msubsup><mi>f</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mtext> </mtext><mi>d</mi><mi>x</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>F</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>−</mo><mi>F</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>a</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\int_a^b f(x)\,dx = F(b) - F(a)

<!--StartFragment--><h3 class="text-text-100 mt-3 -mb-1 text-[1.125rem] font-bold">∫ Calculus</h3>
<ul class="[li_&amp;]:mb-0 [li_&amp;]:mt-1 [li_&amp;]:gap-1 [&amp;:not(:last-child)_ul]:pb-1 [&amp;:not(:last-child)_ol]:pb-1 list-disc flex flex-col gap-1 pl-8 mb-3">
<li class="font-claude-response-body whitespace-normal break-words pl-2"><strong>Derivative (Power Rule):</strong> <span class="katex" role="math"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="\dfrac{d}{dx}x^n = nx^{n-1}"></span></span></span></li>
<li class="font-claude-response-body whitespace-normal break-words pl-2"><strong>Chain Rule:</strong> <span class="katex" role="math"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="\dfrac{d}{dx}f(g(x)) = f'(g(x)) \cdot g'(x)"></span></span></span></li>
<li class="font-claude-response-body whitespace-normal break-words pl-2"><strong>Integration (Power Rule):</strong> <span class="katex" role="math"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="\int x^n\,dx = \dfrac{x^{n+1}}{n+1} + C"></span></span></span></li>
<li class="font-claude-response-body whitespace-normal break-words pl-2"><strong>Fundamental Theorem:</strong> <span class="katex" role="math"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="\int_a^b f(x)\,dx = F(b) - F(a)"></span></span></span></li></ul><!--EndFragment-->

</body></html>

electrical engineering, understanding the relationship between voltage, current, and resistance is essential for designing and analyzing circuits. One of the most fundamental principles is Ohm’s Law, which states that the voltage across a conductor is directly proportional to the current flowing through it. This relationship is represented by:</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mi>V</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>I</mi><mi>R</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">V = IR</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">V</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">I</span><span class="mord mathnormal">R</span></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="434" data-end="631">where <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>V</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">V</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">V</span></span></span></span> represents voltage, <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>I</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">I</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">I</span></span></span></span> represents current, and <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>R</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">R</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">R</span></span></span></span> represents resistance. Using this formula, engineers can calculate unknown electrical values in both simple and complex circuits.</p>
<p data-start="633" data-end="829">Another important concept is electrical power consumption. The power used by an electrical device depends on the voltage applied and the current flowing through it. The standard power equation is:</p>
<p data-start="831" data-end="868"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>P</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>V</mi><mi>I</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">P = VI</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">P</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">V</span><span class="mord mathnormal">I</span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="870" data-end="1084">where <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>P</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">P</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">P</span></span></span></span> is power measured in watts. Combining Ohm’s Law with the power equation also gives alternative forms such as <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>P</mi><mo>=</mo><msup><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msup><mi>R</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">P = I^2R</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">P</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">I</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathnormal">R</span></span></span></span> and <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>P</mi><mo>=</mo><mfrac><msup><mi>V</mi><mn>2</mn></msup><mi>R</mi></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">P = \frac{V^2}{R}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">P</span><span <p data-start="1086" data-end="1335">In alternating current (AC) systems, the frequency and time period of a waveform are related mathematically. Electrical signals in homes and industries commonly operate at fixed frequencies such as 50 Hz or 60 Hz. Their relationship is expressed as:</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mi>T</mi></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">f = \frac{1}{T}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">f</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">T</span></span></span><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="frac-line"></span></span><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="1379" data-end="1560">where <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>f</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">f</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">f</span></span></span></span> is frequency and <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>T</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">T</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">T</span></span></span></span> is the time period of one complete cycle. This equation is important in signal processing, communication systems, and power transmission networks.</p>
<p data-start="1562" data-end="1752">The energy stored in a capacitor is another critical topic in electronics. Capacitors store electrical energy in the form of an electric field, and the stored energy can be calculated using:</p>
<p data-start="1754" data-end="1791"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>E</mi><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mn>2</mn></mfrac><mi>C</mi><msup><mi>V</mi><mn>2</mn></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">E = \frac{1}{2}CV^2</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">E</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="frac-line"></span></span><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span><span class="mord mathnormal">C</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">V</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="1793" data-end="1954" data-is-last-node="" data-is-only-node="">where <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>E</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">E</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">E</span></span></span></span> is energy, <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">C</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">C</span></span></span></span> is capacitance, and <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>V</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">V</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">V</span></span></span></span> is voltage. This principle is used in power supplies, filtering circuits, and energy storage applications.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="z-0 flex min-h-[46px] justify-start"></div></div></div></section><div class="contents"></div></div></div></div><div aria-hidden="true" class="pointer-events-none -mt-px h-px translate-y-[calc(var(--scroll-root-safe-area-inset-bottom)-14*var(--spacing))]"></div><!--EndFragment-->

Combining Ohm’s Law with the power equation also gives alternative forms such as <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="P = I^2R"></span></span></span> and <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="P = \frac{V^2}{R}"></span></span></span>, which are widely used in resistor power calculations.</p>
<p data-start="1086" data-end="1335">In alternating current (AC) systems, the frequency and time period of a waveform are related mathematically. Electrical signals in homes and industries commonly operate at fixed frequencies such as 50 Hz or 60 Hz. Their relationship is expressed as:</p>
<span class="block text-center"><span class="soukKW_collapsedBlockMath relative inline-block align-middle"><span><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="f = \frac{1}{T}"></span></span></span></span></span><button aria-label="Show graph" class="bg-token-bg-tertiary text-token-text-secondary hover:text-token-icon-accent hover:bg-token-icon-accent/20 inline-flex aspect-square h-4 w-4 items-center justify-center rounded-full absolute start-full top-1/2 ms-1 -translate-y-1/2" data-state="closed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="icon-xs w-2.5"><path d="M3 3v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h16"></path><path d="M7 16c.5-2 1.5-7 4-7 2 0 2 3 4 3 2.5 0 4.5-5 5-7"></path></svg></button></span></span>
<p data-start="1379" data-end="1560">where <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="f"></span></span></span> is frequency and <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="T"></span></span></span> is the time period of one complete cycle. This equation is important in signal processing, communication systems, and power transmission networks.</p>
<p data-start="1562" data-end="1752">The energy stored in a capacitor is another critical topic in electronics. Capacitors store electrical energy in the form of an electric field, and the stored energy can be calculated using:</p>
<p data-start="1754" data-end="1791"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="E = \frac{1}{2}CV^2"></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="1793" data-end="1954" data-is-last-node="" data-is-only-node="">where <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="E"></span></span></span> is energy, <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="C"></span></span></span> is capacitance, and <span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="V"></span></span></span> is voltage. This principle is used in power supplies, filtering circuits, and energy storage applications.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="z-0 flex min-h-[46px] justify-start"></div></div></div></section><div class="contents"></div></div></div></div><div aria-hidden="true" class="pointer-events-none -mt-px h-px translate-y-[calc(var(--scroll-root-safe-area-inset-bottom)-14*var(--spacing))]"></div><!--EndFragment-->

</body></html>

<!--StartFragment--><hr data-start="227" data-end="230">
<h2 data-section-id="1dkflnp" data-start="232" data-end="243">Abstract</h2>
<p data-start="245" data-end="1054">Traffic congestion has become a major issue in urban areas due to the rapid increase in vehicle population. Traditional traffic management systems are unable to efficiently control dynamic traffic conditions. This paper proposes an Artificial Intelligence (AI)-based smart traffic management system using machine learning algorithms to optimize traffic signal timing and reduce congestion. The proposed system collects real-time traffic data using cameras and IoT sensors, processes the data using machine learning models, and dynamically adjusts traffic signals. Experimental results show that the proposed approach reduces average waiting time by 35% and improves traffic flow efficiency by 28%. The system can be implemented in smart cities to improve transportation efficiency and reduce fuel consumption.</p>
<p data-start="1056" data-end="1160"><strong data-start="1056" data-end="1069">Keywords:</strong> Artificial Intelligence, Machine Learning, Smart Traffic System, IoT, Traffic Optimization</p><!--EndFragment-->
</body>
</html>

<!--StartFragment--><h1 data-section-id="ywuu3l" data-start="1167" data-end="1184">INTRODUCTION</h1>
<p data-start="1186" data-end="1588">Urban transportation systems face significant challenges due to increasing traffic density and inefficient road management. Conventional traffic systems operate on predefined timers, which cannot adapt to real-time traffic conditions. Intelligent traffic systems powered by AI and machine learning can improve transportation efficiency by analyzing live traffic patterns and making automated decisions.</p>
<p data-start="1590" data-end="1970">Machine learning techniques enable predictive analysis of traffic congestion and dynamic signal control. Recent developments in IoT devices and cloud computing have further enhanced the capability of smart transportation systems. The objective of this research is to develop an intelligent traffic management system capable of minimizing congestion and improving road utilization.</p><!--EndFragment-->
</body>

data-end="3438">The architecture of the proposed smart traffic management system consists of multiple interconnected modules that work together to monitor and optimize traffic flow.</p>
<h3 data-section-id="bcgn0w" data-start="3440" data-end="3463">A. Data Acquisition</h3>
<p data-start="3465" data-end="3614">Traffic data is collected using cameras, infrared sensors, GPS modules, and IoT devices installed at road intersections. The collected data includes:</p>
<ul data-start="3616" data-end="3697">
<li data-section-id="29t5ub" data-start="3616" data-end="3631">
Vehicle count
</li>
<li data-section-id="1tbbr6q" data-start="3632" data-end="3647">
Traffic speed
</li>
<li data-section-id="19xd64x" data-start="3648" data-end="3664">
Lane occupancy
</li>
<li data-section-id="9og3a" data-start="3665" data-end="3679">
Waiting time
</li>
<li data-section-id="yvg1lp" data-start="3680" data-end="3697">
Traffic density
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="3699" data-end="3788">The collected information is transmitted to the cloud server for processing and analysis.</p>
<h3 data-section-id="1dqah12" data-start="3790" data-end="3815">B. Data Preprocessing</h3>
<p data-start="3817" data-end="4035">Raw traffic data often contains noise, missing values, and inconsistencies. Data preprocessing techniques such as normalization, filtering, and feature extraction are applied before training the machine learning model.</p>
<p data-start="4037" data-end="4071">The normalization formula used is:</p>

<p data-start="4112" data-end="4174">This process improves prediction accuracy and model stability.</p>
<h3 data-section-id="76iue4" data-start="4176" data-end="4207">C. Traffic Prediction Model</h3>
<p data-start="4209" data-end="4382">The machine learning model predicts traffic congestion levels using historical and live traffic data. Linear regression and neural networks are used for prediction analysis.</p>
<p data-start="4384" data-end="4428">The cost function for model optimization is:</p>
<p data-start="4430" data-end="4467"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mrow><mn>2</mn><mi>m</mi></mrow></mfrac><msubsup><mo>∑</mo><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><mi>m</mi></msubsup><mo class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen mathnormal mtight">m</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">θ</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mopen mtight">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">i</span><span class="mclose mtight">)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">y</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mopen class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="4469" data-end="4475">Where:</p>
<ul data-start="4477" data-end="4621">
<li data-section-id="1c21znq" data-start="4477" data-end="4512">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">J(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">J</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">θ</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span> = Cost function
</li>
<li data-section-id="n3xd6w" data-start="4513" data-end="4554">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span> = Number of training examples
</li>
<li data-section-id="iwju8t" data-start="4555" data-end="4594">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>h</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">h_\theta(x)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">h</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">θ</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span> = Predicted value
</li>
<li data-section-id="1utrgw8" data-start="4595" data-end="4621">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>y</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">y</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">y</span></span></span></span> = Actual value
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="4623" data-end="4680">The neural network activation function is represented as:</p>
<p data-start="4682" data-end="4719"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>=</mo><mi>max</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">f(x)=\max(0,x)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">f</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mop">max</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">0</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="4721" data-end="4839">This Rectified Linear Unit (ReLU) activation function improves computational efficiency during deep learning training.</p>
<h3 data-section-id="3otmer" data-start="4841" data-end="4867">D. Signal Optimization</h3>
<p data-start="4869" data-end="5080">Based on predicted congestion levels, traffic signal timing is dynamically adjusted. Roads with higher traffic density are allocated longer green signal durations to reduce waiting time and improve traffic flow.</p>
<hr data-start="5082" data-end="5085">
<h2 data-section-id="1cguioh" data-start="5087" data-end="5139">Expanded Content for “IV. RESULTS AND DISCUSSION”</h2>
<p data-start="5141" data-end="5348">The experimental evaluation was conducted using simulated urban traffic datasets collected from multiple intersections. The proposed AI-based system was compared with conventional fixed-time traffic systems.</p>
<p data-start="5350" data-end="5394">The performance evaluation metrics included:</p>
<ul data-start="5396" data-end="5508">
<li data-section-id="uk19p" data-start="5396" data-end="5426">
Average vehicle waiting time
</li>
<li data-section-id="1ojvh1r" data-start="5427" data-end="5447">
Traffic throughput
</li>
<li data-section-id="vdz074" data-start="5448" data-end="5469">

</li>
<li data-section-id="7ikenr" data-start="5470" data-end="5488">

</li>
<li data-section-id="1ygb0u9" data-start="5489" data-end="5508">

</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="5510" data-end="5610">The prediction accuracy of the machine learning model was calculated using Mean Squared Error (MSE):</p>
<p data-start="5612" data-end="5649"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math <p data-start="5651" data-end="5902">The experimental results demonstrate that the proposed system significantly reduces traffic congestion during peak hours. The adaptive signal timing mechanism effectively responds to real-time traffic conditions, improving road utilization efficiency.</p>
<p data-start="5904" data-end="6152">Additionally, the implementation of AI-based traffic prediction reduces fuel wastage caused by unnecessary vehicle idling at intersections. The proposed model also contributes to reducing carbon emissions and improving environmental sustainability.</p>
<p data-start="6154" data-end="6285" data-is-last-node="" data-is-only-node="">The system achieved an overall traffic efficiency improvement of approximately 28% compared to traditional traffic control methods.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="z-0 flex min-h-[46px] justify-start"></div></div></div></section><div class="contents"></div></div></div></div><div aria-hidden="true" class="pointer-events-none -mt-px h-px translate-y-[calc(var(--scroll-root-safe-area-inset-bottom)-14*var(--spacing))]"></div><!--EndFragment-->

class="flex max-w-full flex-col gap-4 grow"><div data-message-author-role="assistant" data-message-id="d85c2373-fa10-45eb-9134-e7184dca9a4b" dir="auto" data-message-model-slug="gpt-5-5" class="min-h-8 text-message relative flex w-full flex-col items-end gap-2 text-start break-words whitespace-normal outline-none keyboard-focused:focus-ring [.text-message+&amp;]:mt-1" data-turn-start-message="true" tabindex="0"><div class="flex w-full flex-col gap-1 empty:hidden"><div class="markdown prose dark:prose-invert wrap-break-word w-full dark markdown-new-styling"><p data-start="3273" data-end="3438">The architecture of the proposed smart traffic management system consists of multiple interconnected modules that work together to monitor and optimize traffic flow.</p>
<h3 data-section-id="bcgn0w" data-start="3440" data-end="3463">A. Data Acquisition</h3>
<p data-start="3465" data-end="3614">Traffic data is collected using cameras, infrared sensors, GPS modules, and IoT devices installed at road intersections. The collected data includes:</p>
<ul data-start="3616" data-end="3697">
<li data-section-id="29t5ub" data-start="3616" data-end="3631">
Vehicle count
</li>
<li data-section-id="1tbbr6q" data-start="3632" data-end="3647">
Traffic speed
</li>
<li data-section-id="19xd64x" data-start="3648" data-end="3664">
Lane occupancy
</li>
<li data-section-id="9og3a" data-start="3665" data-end="3679">
Waiting time
</li>
<li data-section-id="yvg1lp" data-start="3680" data-end="3697">
Traffic density
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="3699" data-end="3788">The collected information is transmitted to the cloud server for processing and analysis.</p>
<h3 data-section-id="1dqah12" data-start="3790" data-end="3815">B. Data Preprocessing</h3>
<p data-start="3817" data-end="4035">Raw traffic data often contains noise, missing values, and inconsistencies. Data preprocessing techniques such as normalization, filtering, and feature extraction are applied before training the machine learning model.</p>
<p data-start="4037" data-end="4071">The normalization formula used is:</p>
<p data-start="4073" data-end="4110"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="x' = \frac{x - x_{min}}{x_{max} - x_{min}}"></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="4112" data-end="4174">This process improves prediction accuracy and model stability.</p>
<h3 data-section-id="76iue4" data-start="4176" data-end="4207">C. Traffic Prediction Model</h3>
<p data-start="4209" data-end="4382">The machine learning model predicts traffic congestion levels using historical and live traffic data. Linear regression and neural networks are used for prediction analysis.</p>
<p data-start="4384" data-end="4428">The cost function for model optimization is:</p>
<p data-start="4430" data-end="4467"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="J(\theta)=\frac{1}{2m}\sum_{i=1}^{m}(h_\theta(x^{(i)})-y^{(i)})^2"></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="4469" data-end="4475">Where:</p>
<ul data-start="4477" data-end="4621">
<li data-section-id="1c21znq" data-start="4477" data-end="4512">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="J(\theta)"></span></span></span> = Cost function
</li>
<li data-section-id="n3xd6w" data-start="4513" data-end="4554">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="m"></span></span></span> = Number of training examples
</li>
<li data-section-id="iwju8t" data-start="4555" data-end="4594">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="h_\theta(x)"></span></span></span> = Predicted value
</li>
<li data-section-id="1utrgw8" data-start="4595" data-end="4621">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="y"></span></span></span> = Actual value
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="4623" data-end="4680">The neural network activation function is represented as:</p>
<p data-start="4682" data-end="4719"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="f(x)=\max(0,x)"></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="4721" data-end="4839">This Rectified Linear Unit (ReLU) activation function improves computational efficiency during deep learning training.</p>
<h3 data-section-id="3otmer" data-start="4841" data-end="4867">D. Signal Optimization</h3>
<p data-start="4869" data-end="5080">Based on predicted congestion levels, traffic signal timing is dynamically adjusted. Roads with higher traffic density are allocated longer green signal durations to reduce waiting time and improve traffic flow.</p>
<hr data-start="5082" data-end="5085">
<h2 data-section-id="1cguioh" data-start="5087" data-end="5139">Expanded Content for “IV. RESULTS AND DISCUSSION”</h2>
<p data-start="5141" data-end="5348">The experimental evaluation was conducted using simulated urban traffic datasets collected from multiple intersections. The proposed AI-based system was compared with conventional fixed-time traffic systems.</p>
<p data-start="5350" data-end="5394">The performance evaluation metrics included:</p>
<ul data-start="5396" data-end="5508">
<li data-section-id="uk19p" data-start="5396" data-end="5426">
Average vehicle waiting time
</li>
<li data-section-id="1ojvh1r" data-start="5427" data-end="5447">
Traffic throughput
</li>
<li data-section-id="vdz074" data-start="5448" data-end="5469">
Prediction accuracy
</li>
<li data-section-id="7ikenr" data-start="5470" data-end="5488">
Fuel consumption
</li>
<li data-section-id="1ygb0u9" data-start="5489" data-end="5508">
Signal efficiency
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="5510" data-end="5610">The prediction accuracy of the machine learning model was calculated using Mean Squared Error (MSE):</p>
<p data-start="5612" data-end="5649"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="MSE = \frac{1}{n}\sum_{i=1}^{n}(y_i - \hat{y}_i)^2"></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="5651" data-end="5902">The experimental results demonstrate that the proposed system significantly reduces traffic congestion during peak hours. The adaptive signal timing mechanism effectively responds to real-time traffic conditions, improving road utilization efficiency.</p>
<p data-start="5904" data-end="6152">Additionally, the implementation of AI-based traffic prediction reduces fuel wastage caused by unnecessary vehicle idling at intersections. The proposed model also contributes to reducing carbon emissions and improving environmental sustainability.</p>
<p data-start="6154" data-end="6285" data-is-last-node="" data-is-only-node="">The system achieved an overall traffic efficiency improvement of approximately 28% compared to traditional traffic control methods.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="z-0 flex min-h-[46px] justify-start"></div></div></div></section><div class="contents"></div></div></div></div><div aria-hidden="true" class="pointer-events-none -mt-px h-px translate-y-[calc(var(--scroll-root-safe-area-inset-bottom)-14*var(--spacing))]"></div><!--EndFragment-->

class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mopen mtight">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">i</span><span class="mclose mtight">)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="4469" data-end="4475">Where:</p>
<ul data-start="4477" data-end="4621">
<li data-section-id="1c21znq" data-start="4477" data-end="4512">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>θ</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">J(\theta)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">J</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">θ</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span> = Cost function
</li>
<li data-section-id="n3xd6w" data-start="4513" data-end="4554">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span> = Number of training examples
</li>
<li data-section-id="iwju8t" data-start="4555" data-end="4594">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>h</mi><mi>θ</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">h_\theta(x)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">h</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span><span class="pstrut"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">θ</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span> = Predicted value
</li>
<li data-section-id="1utrgw8" data-start="4595" data-end="4621">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>y</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">y</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">y</span></span></span></span> = Actual value
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="4623" data-end="4680">The neural network activation function is represented as:</p>
<p data-start="4682" data-end="4719"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>=</mo><mi>max</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">f(x)=\max(0,x)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">f</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut"></span><span class="mop">max</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">0</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">x</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="4721" data-end="4839">This Rectified Linear Unit (ReLU) activation function improves computational efficiency during deep learning training.</p>
<h3 data-section-id="3otmer" data-start="4841" data-end="4867">D. Signal Optimization</h3>
<p data-start="4869" data-end="5080">Based on predicted congestion levels, traffic signal timing is dynamically adjusted. Roads with higher traffic density are allocated longer green signal durations to reduce waiting time and improve traffic flow.</p><!--EndFragment-->
</body>
</html>

TRANSFORMED:

<!--StartFragment--><p data-start="3273" data-end="3438">The architecture of the proposed smart traffic management system consists of multiple interconnected modules that work together to monitor and optimize traffic flow.</p>
<h3 data-section-id="bcgn0w" data-start="3440" data-end="3463">A. Data Acquisition</h3>
<p data-start="3465" data-end="3614">Traffic data is collected using cameras, infrared sensors, GPS modules, and IoT devices installed at road intersections. The collected data includes:</p>
<ul data-start="3616" data-end="3697">
<li data-section-id="29t5ub" data-start="3616" data-end="3631">
Vehicle count
</li>
<li data-section-id="1tbbr6q" data-start="3632" data-end="3647">
Traffic speed
</li>
<li data-section-id="19xd64x" data-start="3648" data-end="3664">
Lane occupancy
</li>
<li data-section-id="9og3a" data-start="3665" data-end="3679">
Waiting time
</li>
<li data-section-id="yvg1lp" data-start="3680" data-end="3697">
Traffic density
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="3699" data-end="3788">The collected information is transmitted to the cloud server for processing and analysis.</p>
<h3 data-section-id="1dqah12" data-start="3790" data-end="3815">B. Data Preprocessing</h3>
<p data-start="3817" data-end="4035">Raw traffic data often contains noise, missing values, and inconsistencies. Data preprocessing techniques such as normalization, filtering, and feature extraction are applied before training the machine learning model.</p>
<p data-start="4037" data-end="4071">The normalization formula used is:</p>
<p data-start="4073" data-end="4110"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="x' = \frac{x - x_{min}}{x_{max} - x_{min}}"></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="4112" data-end="4174">This process improves prediction accuracy and model stability.</p>
<h3 data-section-id="76iue4" data-start="4176" data-end="4207">C. Traffic Prediction Model</h3>
<p data-start="4209" data-end="4382">The machine learning model predicts traffic congestion levels using historical and live traffic data. Linear regression and neural networks are used for prediction analysis.</p>
<p data-start="4384" data-end="4428">The cost function for model optimization is:</p>
<p data-start="4430" data-end="4467"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="J(\theta)=\frac{1}{2m}\sum_{i=1}^{m}(h_\theta(x^{(i)})-y^{(i)})^2"></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="4469" data-end="4475">Where:</p>
<ul data-start="4477" data-end="4621">
<li data-section-id="1c21znq" data-start="4477" data-end="4512">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="J(\theta)"></span></span></span> = Cost function
</li>
<li data-section-id="n3xd6w" data-start="4513" data-end="4554">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="m"></span></span></span> = Number of training examples
</li>
<li data-section-id="iwju8t" data-start="4555" data-end="4594">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="h_\theta(x)"></span></span></span> = Predicted value
</li>
<li data-section-id="1utrgw8" data-start="4595" data-end="4621">
<span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="y"></span></span></span> = Actual value
</li>
</ul>
<p data-start="4623" data-end="4680">The neural network activation function is represented as:</p>
<p data-start="4682" data-end="4719"><span class="inline-block align-middle"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><span data-latex="f(x)=\max(0,x)"></span></span></span></span></p>
<p data-start="4721" data-end="4839">This Rectified Linear Unit (ReLU) activation function improves computational efficiency during deep learning training.</p>
<h3 data-section-id="3otmer" data-start="4841" data-end="4867">D. Signal Optimization</h3>
<p data-start="4869" data-end="5080">Based on predicted congestion levels, traffic signal timing is dynamically adjusted. Roads with higher traffic density are allocated longer green signal durations to reduce waiting time and improve traffic flow.</p><!--EndFragment-->

<h1>Generative AI in 2026: From Chatbots to Colleagues</h1><p>Generative AI has crossed a decisive threshold. What began as a wave of impressive demos and experimental chatbots has matured into foundational infrastructure reshaping how businesses operate, how scientists discover, and how individuals work. Here's where things stand today.</p><h2>The Big Shift: From Tools to Agents</h2><p>Between 2023 and 2025, the big story was raw model capability. In 2026, it is end-to-end agency. Models don't just generate content they observe context, decide what to do, and act across tools and channels.</p><p>Multi-agent orchestration has moved from research papers into production, with co-ordinated AI "teams" handling tasks such as candidate screening, sales operations, and code refactoring pipelines. Think of it less as asking an AI a question and more as delegating a project to a digital colleague.</p><h2>Who's Using It and How Much</h2><p>The adoption numbers are striking. 88% of organizations are now using AI in at least one business function, and 71% are regularly using generative AI specifically.</p>

ORIGINAL:
<hr>
<h1>Generative AI in 2026: From Chatbots to Colleagues</h1>
<p>Generative AI has crossed a decisive threshold. What began as a wave of impressive demos and experimental chatbots has matured into foundational infrastructure reshaping how businesses operate, how scientists discover, and how individuals work. Here's where things stand today.</p>
<h2>The Big Shift: From Tools to Agents</h2>
<p>Between 2023 and 2025, the big story was raw model capability. In 2026, it is end-to-end agency. Models don't just generate content they observe context, decide what to do, and act across tools and channels.</p>
<p>Multi-agent orchestration has moved from research papers into production, with co-ordinated AI "teams" handling tasks such as candidate screening, sales operations, and code refactoring pipelines. Think of it less as asking an AI a question and more as delegating a project to a digital colleague.</p>
<h2>Who's Using It and How Much</h2>
<p>The adoption numbers are striking. 88% of organizations are now using AI in at least one business function, and 71% are regularly using generative AI specifically.</p>

TRANSFORMED:
<hr>
<h1>Generative AI in 2026: From Chatbots to Colleagues</h1>
<p>Generative AI has crossed a decisive threshold. What began as a wave of impressive demos and experimental chatbots has matured into foundational infrastructure reshaping how businesses operate, how scientists discover, and how individuals work. Here's where things stand today.</p>
<h2>The Big Shift: From Tools to Agents</h2>
<p>Between 2023 and 2025, the big story was raw model capability. In 2026, it is end-to-end agency. Models don't just generate content they observe context, decide what to do, and act across tools and channels.</p>
<p>Multi-agent orchestration has moved from research papers into production, with co-ordinated AI "teams" handling tasks such as candidate screening, sales operations, and code refactoring pipelines. Think of it less as asking an AI a question and more as delegating a project to a digital colleague.</p>
<h2>Who's Using It and How Much</h2>
<p>The adoption numbers are striking. 88% of organizations are now using AI in at least one business function, and 71% are regularly using generative AI specifically.</p>
